## Page 19

### p19_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Up and Running (Post-Installation)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Setup workflow**||



### p19_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Step|Action|
|---|---|
|1. Ensure that your devices are configured<br>properly for communication and telemetry.|Refer to the guidelines and sample configurations in:<br>Configuration prerequisites for new devices, on page 260<br>Sample Configuration for Cisco NSO Devices, on page 268|
|2. Create user accounts and user roles.|Follow the steps in Manage Users, on page 349 and Create User<br>Roles, on page 352.|



### p19_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**3**|

## Page 20

### p20_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Up and Running (Post-Installation)|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Setup workflow**|



### p20_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Step|Action|
|---|---|
|3. Create credential profiles.|Follow the steps in Create credential profiles, on page 209|
|4. Add the provider(s).|Follow the steps in Add a provider, on page 218.<br>**Note**<br>In case of the single VM deployment of Crosswork Network<br>Controller Advantage tier, the embedded NSO provider is<br>already added and configured during the deployment.|
|5. Validate communications with the<br>provider(s).|Check on the provider's reachability using the steps in Get<br>Provider Details, on page 249|
|6. Import or create tags.|To import them: Import multiple tags using a CSV file, on page<br>256<br>To create them: Create tags, on page 255|
|7. Onboard your devices.|See Add devices to the inventory, on page 259.<br>For more information, see the_ Cisco Crosswork Network_<br>_Controller 7.1 Device Lifecycle Management_ guide.|
|8. Setup Crosswork Data Gateway|For cluster deployment, follow the steps in Set up Crosswork<br>Data Gateway to collect data, on page 51.<br>For single VM deployment, follow the steps in Data collection<br>using Embedded Collectors, on page 148|
|9. Validate Crosswork Network Controller<br>communications with devices.|Review the** Devices** window. All the devices you have onboarded<br>should be reachable.<br>Click<br>to investigate any device whose** Reachability State** is<br>marked as<br>(unreachable),<br>(degraded), or<br>(unknown).<br>For more information, see the_ Cisco Crosswork Network_<br>_Controller 7.1 Device Lifecycle Management_ guide.|
|10. (Optional) Enable source IP for<br>auditing.|If you want to log the user's IP address for auditing and<br>accounting, see Configure AAA Settings, on page 398.|
|11. (Optional) Create additional user<br>accounts and user roles.|Follow the steps in Manage Users, on page 349 and Create User<br>Roles, on page 352.|
|12. (Optional) Import or create additional<br>credential profiles and providers.|To import providers: Import multiple providers using a CSV file,<br>on page 220<br>To create providers: Add a provider, on page 218|
|13. (Optional) Group your devices<br>logically as per your requirement.|Follow the steps in Use Device Groups to Filter your Topology<br>Map, on page 282.|
|14. (Optional) Set display preferences for<br>your topology.|Follow the steps in Use Internal Maps Offline for Geographical<br>Map Display, on page 281 and Show Link Health by Color, on<br>page 303.|

## Page 23

### p23_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Menu option|Description|
|---|---|
|**Actions > Data Backup**<br>(See Manage Crosswork<br>Network Controller<br>Backup and Restore, on<br>page 9 for details)|Preserves the Crosswork Network Controller configuration data. The backup file<br>can be used with the data disaster restore (Restore Crosswork Network Controller<br>After a Disaster, on page 12) to recover from a serious outage.|

## Page 24

### p24_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Backups|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Embedded NSO backup**|



### p24_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Menu option|Description|
|---|---|
|**Actions > Data Disaster**<br>**Restore**<br>(See Restore Crosswork<br>Network Controller After<br>a Disaster, on page 12<br>for details)|Restores the Crosswork Network Controller configuration data after a natural or<br>human-caused disaster has required you to rebuild a Crosswork cluster.<br>First, deploy a new cluster by following the instructions in the_ Cisco Crosswork_<br>_Network Controller 7.1 Installation Guide_. Ensure you install the exact versions<br>of the applications that were in your old Crosswork cluster when you made the<br>data backup. Any version mismatch can lead to data loss and restore job failure.|
|**Actions > Data**<br>**Migration**<br>(See Migrate data using<br>backup and restore, on<br>page 20 for details)|Migrates data from an older version of Crosswork Network Controller to a newer<br>version.|



### p24_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Backup Type|From Deployment|To Deployment|Support|
|---|---|---|---|
|Data only|Geo redundant|Geo redundant|Supported|
|Data only|Non-geo redundant|Non-geo redundant|Supported|

### p40_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|---|---|
|Navigation|Use the** Crosswork Manager** window to check the health of the cluster. To display<br>this window, from the main menu, choose** Administration** >** Crosswork Manager**.|
|**Crosswork**<br>**Summary** window|The** Crosswork Manager** window gives you summary information about the status<br>of the nodes, the Platform Infrastructure, and the applications you have installed.|

## Page 41

### p41_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage the Crosswork Cluster|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Cluster management overview**||



### p41_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Action|Description|
|---|---|
|**Cluster**<br>**Management**<br>window<br>**Note**<br>Can be viewed only<br>when Crosswork<br>Network Controller<br>is deployed as a<br>cluster.|Click on the** System Summary** tile to see the details of the nodes in the cluster.<br>The top left section of the window provides details about the cluster while the top right<br>provides details about overall cluster resource consumption. The bottom section breaks<br>down the resource utilization by node, with a separate detail tile for each node. The<br>window shows other details, including the IP addresses in use, whether each node is<br>a hybrid or worker, and so on.<br>**Note**<br>When the Crosswork Network Controller is deployed on AWS EC2, the VM status<br>initially appears as "unknown" by default. If you update the inventory file, the status<br>changes to "initializing." This behavior is normal for EC2 deployments.<br>On the top-right corner, click the** View more visualizations** link to Visually Monitor<br>System Functions in Real Time, on page 412.<br>To see details for a specific node, click<br>on the tile of the node, and choose** View**<br>**Details**. The VM Node window displays the node details, including the list of<br>components, microservices, and alarms running on the node.<br>• To request metrics or logs, click<br>under the** Action** column, and select the<br>relevant option.<br>• To restart a microservice, click<br>under the** Action** column, and choose** Restart**.<br>For information on how to use the** Crosswork Health** tab, see Monitor platform<br>infrastructure and application health, on page 412.|
|**System Summary**<br>window|**Note**<br>Applicable only when Crosswork is deployed on a single VM.<br>Click on the** System Summary** tile to see the VM details.|

## Page 64

### p64_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Data Gateway user interface components**|



### p64_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Column|Description|
|---|---|
|**Operational State**|Operational state of the Data Gateway instance.<br>A Data Gateway has the following operational states:<br>• Degraded: The Data Gateway is reachable but one or more of its<br>components are in a state other than OK.<br>• Up: The Data Gateway is operational and all individual components<br>are OK.<br>• Error: The Data Gateway instance is unreachable or some of its<br>components are in Error state.|
|**Administration state**|Administration state of the Data Gateway instance. The state could be<br>any of the following:<br>• Up: The instance is administratively up.<br>• Maintenance: Operations between Cisco Crosswork and Data<br>Gateway are suspended to perform upgrades or other maintenance<br>activities (for example, uploading certificates).<br>• Patch in-progress: The process of installing or applying a patch on<br>the Data Gateway is currently ongoing.<br>• Patch failed: The process of installing or applying a patch on the<br>Data Gateway failed.|
|**High availability status**|High availability status of a Data Gateway could be either:<br>• Protected: All instances are in the UP state, and the number of<br>standby instances in the pool matches the number of active<br>instances.<br>• Not protected: All standby instances are DOWN.<br>• Limited protection: At least one standby instance in the pool is in<br>the UP state.<br>• None planned: No standby instances were added to the pool during<br>pool creation.|
|**Devices**|Number of devices that are attached to the Data Gateway pool.|



### p64_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**48**|||



---

## Page 65

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Data Gateway user interface components**||



### p65_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Column|Description|
|---|---|
|**Name**|Name of the Data Gateway instance.<br>Clicking the<br>icon next to the name displays the enrollment details<br>of each instance. This includes details such as the:<br>• Virtual IP Addresses<br>• Data Gateway Instance Name<br>• Description<br>• Data Gateway Instance Type that indicates the profile of Data<br>Gateway.<br>• Data Gateway Instance UUID<br>Click the instance name to open the Data Gateway vitals page. The page<br>displays the operations and health summary of a Data Gateway.|
|**Pool name**|Name of the Data Gateway pool. On clicking the pool name, the Data<br>Gateway vitals page opens.|
|**Site name**|Site to which the Data Gateway instance is assigned.<br>**Note**<br>This column is only displayed with the geo redundancy feature enabled.<br>For information on the geo redundancy capabilities, see the_ Enable Geo_<br>_Redundancy_ section in the_ Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1_<br>_Installation Guide_.|
|**Data gateway instance role**|Indicates the current role of the Data Gateway instance. The role could<br>be any of the following:<br>• Assigned: The Data Gateway instance is attached to a pool.<br>• Unassigned: The Data Gateway instance is not attached to any pool.<br>• Spare (Active): The Data Gateway instance is a spare instance that<br>is used during failover process in an active site.<br>• Spare (Standby): The Data Gateway instance acts as a spare instance<br>for failover procedures in a standby site.|

## Page 66

### p66_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Data Gateway user interface components**|



### p66_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Column|Description|
|---|---|
|**Outage history**|Outage history of the Data Gateway instance over a period of 14 days.<br>State aggregation for a day is done in the order of precedence as Error,<br>Degraded, Up, Unknown and Not Ready.<br>For example, if the Data Gateway instance went Unknown to Degraded<br>to Up, the color is displayed as Degraded (orange) for that day as<br>Degraded takes precedence over Up and Unknown.<br>If the Data Gateway was in Error state at any time during that day, the<br>tile is Red. If the Data Gateway was not in Error but in Degraded State<br>anytime of the day, the tile is Orange. If the Data Gateway was not in<br>Error or Degraded state and was only Up, then the tile is Green.|
|**Average availability**|Value indicating the health of the Data Gateway instance. This percentage<br>is calculated as the total time (in milliseconds) a Data Gateway was in<br>the UP state over the time between start time of first event and end time<br>of last event.<br>**Note**<br>The end time of the last event is the current timestamp, so the duration<br>of the last event is between its start time and the current timestamp.|
|**Data gateway instance name**|Name of the Data Gateway that is created automatically when you add<br>a Data Gateway instance to a pool.<br>Clicking the<br>icon next to the instance name displays the enrollment<br>details of each instance. This includes details such as the:<br>• Instance name, type, role, UUID, OS version<br>• Description<br>• CPU<br>• Memory<br>• Number of NICs<br>• Interface roles, MAC, IPv4 and IPv6 address<br>The** Additional interface role information** describes the interface roles<br>available in Data Gateway.|
|**Attached device count**|Indicates the number of the devices that are attached to the Data Gateway<br>pool.|
|**PDG identifier**|Unique identifier of the physical Data Gateway instance.|

The name<br>can contain a maximum of 128 alphanumeric<br>characters, plus underscores ("_") or hyphens ("-").<br>No other special characters are allowed.<br>If you have many data destinations, make the name<br>as informative as possible to be able to distinguish<br>later.|Yes|Yes|
|**Server type**|From the drop-down, select the server type of your<br>data destination.|Yes|Yes|

|**Compression type**|From the drop-down, select the compression type.|Yes<br>Supported<br>compression types<br>are snappy, gzip, and<br>deflate.|Yes<br>Supported<br>compression types<br>are snappy, gzip,<br>zstd, and none.<br>**Note**<br>zstd compression<br>type is supported<br>only for Kafka 2.0 or<br>higher.|
|**Dispatch Type**|This field is available when the** Server Type** field<br>is set to** gRPC**.<br>From the drop-down, select the dispatch method as<br>stream or unary.<br>Crosswork Data Gateway transmits the collected<br>data to the destination as data streams or unary. The<br>default value is unary.|Yes|No|

## Page 100

### p100_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Considerations for external data destination**|



### p100_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Behavior|Requirement|
|---|---|
|Reinstallation behavior|If you reinstall an existing external Kafka destination using the same IP<br>address, you must restart the collectors for the changes to take effect.|
|Securing the communication<br>channel|You can secure the communication channel between Cisco Crosswork<br>Network Controller or Cisco EPN Manager and the destination<br>(Crosswork Kafka or external Kafka).<br>**Note**<br>Enabling security may impact system performance.|
|TLS requirements and certificate<br>preparation|• If the external destination requires TLS, prepare the following in<br>advance:<br>• Public certificate for server authentication.<br>• Client certificate and key files for mutual authentication.<br>• If the client key is password-encrypted, you must configure the<br>password during data destination provisioning.<br>• Only IP-based certificates are currently supported by Crosswork<br>Data Gateway or EPN Manager Data Gateway.|
|Certificate format guidelines|• Ensure that certificates are PEM-encoded.<br>• Ensure that the key file is in PKCS#8 format when generating<br>certificates via your Certificate Authority (CA).|



### p100_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**84**|||

## Page 101

### p101_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Delete a Data Destination**||



### p101_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Behavior|Requirement|
|---|---|
|Kafka topic preparation|• Create Kafka topics before submitting the job in Cisco Crosswork.<br>• If the topic does not exist, this error may appear in the logs:<br>`destinationContext: topicmdt4`<br>`org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnknownTopicOrPartitionException:`<br>`This server does not`<br>`host this topic-partition.`<br>This typically indicates:<br>• The topic was not created before dispatch.<br>• The topic was deleted before the data collection job completed.|
|Connectivity check|Verify that the port connectivity for the external destination.<br>If the port is unreachable, data collection fails.|
|Kafka destination configuration|Custom values for a Kafka destination can be configured in the<br>destination properties.<br>This feature is not supported for gRPC destinations.|
|Global versus custom properties|• Global properties that are specified in the** Destination Details** pane<br>are mandatory. These are applied to all Kafka destinations by<br>default.<br>• Custom values that are entered at the collector level override global<br>properties, but apply only to that collector.|
|IP address compatibility|The external destination must match the IP version (IPv4 or IPv6)<br>selected during Crosswork Data Gateway deployment.<br>For example, if IPv4 was selected during deployment, the destination<br>must also use IPv4.|
|DNS TTL and hostname updates|Changes to hostname-to-IP mappings take effect on the Data Gateway<br>only after the Time to Live (TTL) duration expires on the DNS server.<br>To apply the changes immediately, it is recommended to reboot the VM.|



### p101_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**85**|

## Page 108

### p108_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Configure Data Collector(s) Global Settings**|



### p108_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Parameter Name|Description|Default value for cluster VM deployment|
|---|---|---|
|**Number of CLI sessions**|Maximum number of CLI sessions between<br>a Crosswork Data Gateway and devices.<br>**Note**<br>This value overrides any internal<br>configuration set for the same parameter.|3<br>Accepted range is 1–50|
|**SSH session timeout**|The session timeout (in seconds) is the<br>duration for which a CLI connection can<br>remain idle in the CLI and SNMP collectors.|120<br>Accepted range is 5–120 seconds|
|**SNMP trap port**|Modify the value as per your deployment<br>environment and configuration requirements.|1062<br>Accepted range is 1–65535|
|**Syslog UDP port**|Modify the value as per your deployment<br>environment and configuration requirements.|9514<br>Accepted range is 1–65535|
|**Syslog TCP port**|-|9898<br>Accepted range is 1–65535|
|**Syslog TLS port**|-|6514<br>Accepted range is 1–65535|
|**Re-Sync SNMPv3 details**|USM details change whenever a device is<br>rebooted or reimaged. SNMPv3 collections<br>stop working whenever there is change in<br>any of the USM details.|Disable<br>By default, this option is disabled for<br>security reasons. Automatic synchronization<br>of updated USM (User Session Manager)<br>information is not permitted to prevent<br>unintended data collection with an incorrect<br>source.<br>When enabled, the system automatically<br>updates USM information after changes,<br>such as hardware updates or device reboots.<br>This ensures that data collection continues<br>without user intervention.<br>If the option remains disabled, you must<br>manually intervene to re-establish USM<br>communication. This can be done by either<br>detaching and reattaching the device to the<br>Crosswork Data Gateway pool or toggling<br>the device's admin state (Down and then<br>Up).|



### p108_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**92**|||

### p116_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Version|Command|To...|
|---|---|---|
|V2c|`snmp-server group`_` <group_name>`_<br>`v2c`<br>`snmp-server user`_` <user_name>`_<br>_`<group_name>`_` v2c`|Define the SNMP version, user/user<br>group details.|
|V2c|`snmp-server host`_` <host_ip>`_<br>`traps`_` SNMP version`_<br>_`<community_string>`_` udp-port`<br>`1062`<br>`snmp-server host a.b.c.d traps`<br>`version 2c v2test udp-port`<br>`1062`|Define the destination to which trap<br>data must be forwarded.<br>**Note**<br>The IP address mentioned here<br>must be the virtual IP address of<br>the Crosswork Data Gateway.|
|V2c|`snmp-server traps snmp linkup`<br>`snmp-server traps snmp`<br>`linkdown`|Enable traps to notify link status.|

### p117_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Version|Command|To...|
|---|---|---|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server host`_` <host_IP>`_<br>`traps version 3 priv`<br>_`<user_name>`_` udp-port 1062`|Define the destination to which trap<br>data must be forwarded.<br>**Note**<br>The IP address mentioned here<br>must be the virtual IP address of<br>the Crosswork Data Gateway.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server user`_` <user_name>`_<br>_`<group_name>`_` v3 auth md5`<br>`<password> priv aes 128`<br>`<password>`|Configures the SNMP server group<br>to enable authentication for<br>members of a specified named<br>access list.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server view`_` <user_name>`_<br>_`< MIB >`_` included`|Define what must be reported.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server group`_` <group_name>`_<br>`v3 auth notify`_` <user_name>`_<br>`read`_` <user_name>`_` write`<br>_`<user_name>`_|Define the SNMP version, user/user<br>group details.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server enable traps snmp`<br>`[authentication ] [linkup ]`<br>`[linkdown ] [warmstart ]`<br>`[coldstart ]`|• When used without any of the<br>optional keywords, enables<br>authenticationFailure, linkUp,<br>linkDown, warmStart, and<br>coldStart traps.<br>• When used with keywords,<br>enables only the trap types<br>specified. For example, to<br>globally enable only linkUp<br>and linkDown SNMP traps for<br>all interfaces, use the<br>**snmp-server enable traps**<br>**snmp linkup linkdown** form<br>of this command.|

## Page 134

### p134_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Crosswork Data Gateway|Col2|
|---|---|
||**gNMI Collection Job**|



### p134_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Type|Subtype|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Once|None|Collects and sends the current<br>snapshot of the system<br>configuration only once for all<br>specified paths|
|Stream|SAMPLE|Cadence-based collection.|
|Stream|ON_CHANGE|First response includes the state of<br>all the elements for the subscribed<br>path, followed by subsequent<br>updates to the changes leaf values.|
|Stream|TARGET_DEFINED|Router/Device chooses the mode<br>of subscription on a per-leaf basis<br>based on the subscribed path (i.e.<br>one of SAMPLE or<br>ON_CHANGE)|

From<br>the sensor data summary pop up you can copy the<br>sensor data by clicking** Copy to Clipboard**.<br>Click<br>to see collection/distribution metrics<br>summary. The metrics are reported on cadence-basis<br>i.e., once every 10 minutes by default. It shows the<br>following metrics for a collection:<br>• last_collection_time_msec<br>• total_collection_message_count<br>• last_device_latency_msec<br>• last_collection_cadence_msec<br>It shows the following metrics for a collection:<br>• total_output_message_count<br>• last_destination_latency_msec<br>• last_output_cadence_msec<br>• last_output_time_msec<br>• total_output_bytes_count|
|Destination|Data destination for the job.|

### p165_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Task|Follow the steps in...|
|---|---|
|1. Verify that the default collection jobs are created<br>and running successfully.|Monitor Embedded Collectors Application Health,<br>on page 204|
|2. (Optional) Extend device coverage to collect data<br>from currently unsupported devices or third-party<br>devices.|Device packages, on page 156|

### p178_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Parameter Name|Description|Default value for single VM deployment|
|---|---|---|
|**Number of CLI**<br>**sessions**|Maximum number of CLI sessions that can be<br>set up between an embedded data collector and<br>devices.<br>Change this value to increase or decrease the<br>number of concurrent sessions allowed on the<br>device, based on your requirements.|3<br>Accepted range is 1-50|
|**SSH Session**<br>**Timeout**|The session timeout (in seconds) is the duration<br>for which a CLI connection can remain idle in<br>the CLI and SNMP collectors.|120<br>Accepted range is 1-120 seconds|
|**SNMP Trap Port**|Modify this value as per your deployment<br>environment and configuration requirements.|31062<br>Accepted range is 30160–31560|
|**Syslog UDP Port**|Modify this value as per your deployment<br>environment and configuration requirements.|30514<br>Accepted range is 30160–31560|
|**Syslog TCP Port**|-|30898<br>Accepted range is 30160–31560|

## Page 179

### p179_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|---|---|
|**Configure the global parameters**||



### p179_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Parameter Name|Description|Default value for single VM deployment|
|---|---|---|
|**Syslog TLS Port**|-|30614<br>Accepted range of ports is 30160–31560|
|**Re-Sync SNMPv3**<br>**Details**|USM details change whenever a device is<br>rebooted or reimaged. SNMPV3 collections stop<br>working whenever there is a change in any of the<br>USM details.|Disable<br>By default, this option is disabled for security<br>reasons. Automatic synchronization of updated<br>USM (User Session Manager) information is not<br>permitted to prevent unintended data collection<br>with an incorrect source.<br>When enabled, the system automatically updates<br>USM information after changes, such as hardware<br>updates or device reboots. This ensures that data<br>collection continues without user intervention.<br>If the option remains disabled, you must manually<br>intervene to re-establish USM communication.<br>This can be done by either detaching and<br>reattaching the device to the embedded collectors<br>or toggling the device's admin state (Down and<br>then Up).|

|Version|Command|To...|
|---|---|---|

|V2c|`snmp-server traps snmp linkup`<br>`snmp-server traps snmp`<br>`linkdown`|Enable traps to notify link status.|

### p185_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Version|Command|To...|
|---|---|---|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server host`_` <host_IP>`_<br>`traps version 3 priv`<br>_`<user_name>`_` udp-port 31062`|Define the destination to which trap<br>data must be forwarded.<br>**Note**<br>The IP address mentioned here<br>must be the Data VIP address of<br>Embedded Collectors.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server user`_` <user_name>`_<br>_`<group_name>`_` v3 auth md5`<br>`<password> priv aes 128`<br>`<password>`|Configures the SNMP server group<br>to enable authentication for<br>members of a specified named<br>access list.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server view`_` <user_name>`_<br>_`< MIB >`_` included`|Define what must be reported.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server group`_` <group_name>`_<br>`v3 auth notify`_` <user_name>`_<br>`read`_` <user_name>`_` write`<br>_`<user_name>`_|Define the SNMP version, user/user<br>group details.|
|V3<br>**Note**<br>Password for a SNMPv3 user must<br>be at least 8 bytes.|`snmp-server enable traps snmp`<br>`[authentication ] [linkup ]`<br>`[linkdown ] [warmstart ]`<br>`[coldstart ]`|• When used without any of the<br>optional keywords, enables<br>authenticationFailure, linkUp,<br>linkDown, warmStart, and<br>coldStart traps.<br>• When used with keywords,<br>enables only the trap types<br>specified. For example, to<br>globally enable only linkUp<br>and linkDown SNMP traps for<br>all interfaces, use the<br>**snmp-server enable traps**<br>**snmp linkup linkdown** form<br>of this command.|

|**gNMI collection job**||



### p201_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Type|Subtype|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Once||Collects and sends the current<br>snapshot of the system<br>configuration only once for all<br>specified paths|
|Stream|SAMPLE|Cadence-based collection.|
|Stream|ON_CHANGE|First response includes the state of<br>all the elements for the subscribed<br>path, followed by subsequent<br>updates to the changed leaf values.|
|Stream|TARGET_DEFINED|Router/Device chooses the mode<br>of subscription on a per-leaf basis<br>based on the subscribed path (i.e.<br>one of SAMPLE or<br>ON_CHANGE)|

## Page 227

### p227_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Prepare Infrastructure for Device Management|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Credential profile template guidelines**||



### p227_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Entries|Required or Optional|
|---|---|---|
|**Credential Profile**|The name of the credential profile. For<br>example:** nso**,** srpce**.|Required|
|**Connectivity Type**|Valid values are: SSH, SNMPv2,<br>NETCONF, TELNET, HTTP,<br>HTTPS, GNMI, SNMPv3, or TL1.|Required<br>• Devices—SNMP and SSH (to<br>avoid operational errors due to<br>clock synchronization checks) are<br>required.<br>• SR-PCE—Since SR-PCE is<br>considered a provider and a<br>device, SSH, and HTTP are<br>required.<br>• NSO—NETCONF is required.<br>**Note**<br>SSH and SNMP credentials are<br>mandatory for onboarding devices and<br>synchronizing with the NSO provider.|
|**User Name**|For example: NSOUser|Required if** Connectivity Type** is** SSH**,<br>**NETCONF**,** TELNET**,** HTTP**,<br>**HTTPS**,** SNMPv3**, or** GRPC**.|
|**Password**|The password for the preceding** User**<br>**Name**.|Required|
|**Enable Password**|Use an Enable password. Valid values<br>are:**` ENABLE`**,**` DISABLE`**, or leave<br>blank (unselected)|Required if** Connectivity Type** is** SSH**<br>or** TELNET**. Otherwise leave blank.|
|**Enable Password**<br>**Value**|Specify the Enable password to use.|Required if** Connectivity Type** is** SSH**<br>or** TELNET**, and** Enable Password**<br>is set to**` ENABLE`**. Otherwise leave<br>blank.|

|**SNMPV3 Priv Type**|The following SNMPv3 Privacy<br>Types are supported:<br>• CFB_AES_128<br>• CBC_DES_56<br>• AES-192<br>• AES-256<br>• 3-DES|Required if** Connectivity Type** is<br>**SNMPv3** and** SnmpV3 Security Level**<br>is** AuthPriv**|
|**SNMPV3 Priv**<br>**Password**|The password for this privilege type.|Required if** Connectivity Type** is<br>**SNMPv3** and** SnmpV3 Security Level**<br>is** AuthPriv**|

## Page 235

### p235_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Prepare Infrastructure for Device Management|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Add a provider**||



### p235_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|*** Provider Name**|The name for the provider that will be used to refer to it in the Cisco Crosswork application.<br>For example:**` Linux_Server`**. The name can contain a maximum of 128 alphanumeric<br>characters, plus dots (.), underscores ("_") or hyphens ("-"). No other special characters are<br>allowed.|
|*** Credential Profile**|Select the name of the credential profile that is used by the Cisco Crosswork application to<br>connect to the provider.|
|*** Family**|Select the provider family.|
|**Connection Type(s)**|**Connection Type(s)**|
|*** Protocol**|Select the principal protocol to be used to connect to the provider.<br>To add more connectivity protocols for this provider, click<br>at the end of the first row. To<br>delete a protocol you have entered, click<br>shown next to that row.<br>You can enter as many sets of connectivity details as you want, including multiple sets for the<br>same protocol.|
|*** Server Details**|Select and provide one of the options:<br>• IP Address (IPv4 or IPv6) and subnet mask of the provider's server.<br>• FQDN (Domain name and Host name)|
|*** Port**|Enter the port number to use to connect to the provider's server. This is the port corresponding<br>to the protocol being configured. For example, if the protocol used to communicate with the<br>provider server is SSH, the port number is usually 22.|
|**Timeout**|Enter the amount of time (in seconds) to wait before the connection times out. The default is<br>30 seconds.|
|**Model Prefix Info**<br>**Note**<br>The** Model** and** Version** fields do not apply to single VM deployments of Crosswork Network Controller.|**Model Prefix Info**<br>**Note**<br>The** Model** and** Version** fields do not apply to single VM deployments of Crosswork Network Controller.|



### p235_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|

### p236_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Prepare Infrastructure for Device Management|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Import multiple providers using a CSV file**|



### p236_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|*** Model**|Required if you are adding a Cisco NSO provider: Select the model prefix that matches the<br>NED CLI used by Cisco NSO. Valid values are:<br>**`Cisco-IOS-XR`**<br>**`Cisco-NX-OS`**<br>**`Cisco-IOS-XE`**<br>For telemetry, only**` Cisco-IOS-XR`** is supported.<br>To add more model prefix information for this Cisco NSO provider, click the<br>at the end of<br>any row in the** Model Prefix Info** section. To delete a model prefix you have entered, click<br>the<br>shown next to that row.|
|*** Version**|Required only if you are adding a Cisco NSO provider: Enter the Cisco NSO NED driver<br>version used on the NSO server.|
|**Provider Properties**|**Provider Properties**|
|**Property Key**|Enter the name of the key for the special provider property you want to configure.<br>Provider properties control how the Cisco Crosswork Network Controller component interacts<br>with the provider. Not all providers need them, and the number and type of properties vary<br>with the provider family. These properties are documented in topics about adding specific<br>providers elsewhere in this Guide. The system does not validate provider properties. Make sure<br>the properties you enter are valid for the provider.<br>**Note**<br>In a two network interface configuration, the Cisco Crosswork applications default to<br>communicating with providers using the Management Network Interface (**`eth0`**). You can<br>change this behavior by adding** Property Key** and** Property Value** as**` outgoing-internal`**<br>and**` eth1`** respectively. This is most often necessary when creating the SR-PCE provider, as<br>its management interface may reside on the data network instead of the management network.|
|**Property Value**|Enter the value to assign to the property key.<br>To add more special properties for this provider, click<br>at the end of any key/value pair in<br>the** Provider Properties** section. To delete a key/value pair you have entered, click<br>shown<br>next to that pair.|

||**View Installed NSO Function Packs**|



### p242_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Property Key|Value|
|---|---|
|**`forward`**|**`true`**<br>This property is necessary when using the Cisco Crosswork Network<br>Controller solution to allow provisioning operations within the UI and to<br>enable the northbound interface to NSO via the Crosswork API gateway.<br>**Note**<br>The default value of**` forward`** is "false". If this is not changed, the devices<br>added to Crosswork will not be added to NSO. This setting is used in<br>conjuction with the** Edit Policy** option (see Edit NSO provider policy, on<br>page 227).|
|**`nso_crosslaunch_url`**<br>**Note**<br>This property is used only for NSO<br>standalone provider.|Enter the URL for cross-launching NSO in the format:**` https://<NSO`**<br>**`IP address/FQDN>: port number`**<br>To enable cross-launch of the NSO application from the Crosswork UI.<br>Requires a valid protocol (**`HTTP`** or**` HTTPS`**), and the provider must be<br>reachable.<br>The cross launch icon (<br>) is displayed in the** Provider Name** column.<br>Alternately, you can cross launch the NSO application using the launch icon<br>located at the top right corner of the window.|
|**`input_url_prefix`**<br>**Note**<br>This property is used only for NSO<br>LSA provider.|Enter the RFS ID in the format:**` /rfc-x`**, where**` x`** refers to the number of<br>the RFS node.<br>`Example (for RFS node 1):`<br>`input_url_prefix: /rfc-1`|

## Page 244

### p244_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Prepare Infrastructure for Device Management|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Edit NSO provider policy**|



### p244_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|**Match**|Select** True** to have DLM match the devices in Crosswork with those in NSO based on their IP<br>address. Select** False** if you do not want this matching.|
|**MatchRule**|Enter an expression defining the subset of devices.|
|**Onboard To NSO**|Select** True** to add devices that are missing in NSO. Select** False** if you do not want to add missing<br>devices to NSO.|
|**Onboard To Rule**|Enter an expression for onboarding a subset of devices.|
|**Onboard From**|Select** True** to add devices from NSO to Crosswork if they are missing. Select** False** if you do<br>not want to add missing devices from NSO.|
|**Onboard From**<br>**Rule**|Enter an expression for onboarding devices from NSO.|
|**Sync From**|Select** True** to perform a sync-from operation on the NSO device after onboarding it. Select** False**<br>if you do not want to perform this sync operation.|
|**Sync From Rule**|Enter an expression defining the subset of devices for sync-from.|
|**Check Sync**|Select** True** to check the sync status of an existing NSO device. Select** False** if you do not want<br>to check the sync status.|
|**Check Sync Rule**|Enter an expression for the subset of devices for check-sync.|
|**NED**|Specify the Network Element Driver (NED) to be used. By default, the latest CLI NED on NSO<br>is used.|
|**Rule**|Enter an expression to define which devices should use a specific NED.|



### p244_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**228**|||

## Page 249

### p249_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Prepare Infrastructure for Device Management|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Add SR-PCE providers**||



### p249_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|When the property<br>key is..|And the value is..|Then..|
|---|---|---|
|auto-onboard|off|when devices are discovered, the device data is recorded in the<br>Cisco SR-PCE database, but is not registered in the Crosswork<br>Network Controller Inventory Management database<br>**Note**<br>Use this option if you plan to manually (via UI or CSV import)<br>enter all of your network devices.|
|auto-onboard|unmanaged|all devices that Crosswork Network Controller discovers will be<br>registered in the Crosswork Network Controller Inventory<br>Management database, with their configured state set to<br>**unmanaged**. SNMP polling will be disabled for these devices,<br>and no management IP information will be included. To get these<br>devices into the** managed** state later, you will need to either edit<br>them via the UI or export them to a CSV, make modifications and<br>then import the updated CSV. You can also assign credential<br>profiles by adding them to the device CSV file before import (the<br>credential profiles must already exist).|
|auto-onboard|managed|all devices that Cisco SR-PCE discovers will be registered in the<br>Crosswork Network Controller Inventory Management database<br>with their configured state set to** managed**.<br>Typically suitable for an environment that has same device profiles,<br>devices are managed by their TE router-ID, and all devices can<br>be discovered by the Cisco SR-PCE.<br>SNMP polling will be enabled for these devices, and Cisco<br>SR-PCE will also report the management IP address (TE Router<br>ID for IPv4, or IPv6 Router ID for IPv6 deployment). The devices<br>will be added with the credential profile associated with the<br>device-profile key in the SR-PCE provider configuration.<br>Important considerations<br>If you enable this option for IPv6 deployment, devices will still<br>register as** unmanaged** in the inventory.<br>When you delete an onboarded device that was added via SR-PCE<br>discovery with auto-onboard set to** managed**, the topology service<br>adds it again as** unmanaged**. This ensures that devices that have<br>been removed are not automatically managed again unless they<br>acquire a new TE-ID. To manage a rediscovered device, update<br>its status manually.|
|device-profile|a credential profile<br>name|if the** auto-onboard** is set to** managed** and there is no valid<br>**device-profile** set, the device will instead be onboarded as<br>**unmanaged**.|

### p250_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|When the property<br>key is..|And the value is..|Then..|
|---|---|---|
|outgoing-interface|eth1|this enables Crosswork Network Controller access to SR-PCE via<br>the data network interface when using a two NIC configuration.|
|preferred-stack|ipv4|indicates a dual stack is present and IPv4 is preferred|
|preferred-stack|ipv6|indicates dual stack is present and IPv6 is preferred|
|preferred-stack|NOT SET|indicates no dual stack|
|pce|off|discovery of RSVP-TE tunnels and PCEP sessions (required for<br>all LSP provisioning) is disabled.|
|pce|on|discovery of RSVP-TE tunnels and PCEP sessions (required for<br>all LSP provisioning) is enabled. This option is enabled by default.|
|topology|any value|there is no impact.<br>This property key is deprecated and should be manually removed<br>if it still appears as an option. This property key is ignored,<br>regardless if it is configured.|

### p285_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Onboard Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Add devices through the UI**||



### p285_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|**Device info**|**Device info**|
|*** Admin state**|The management state of the device. Options are<br>•**` UNMANAGED`**—Crosswork Network Controller is not monitoring the device.<br>•**` DOWN`**—The device is being managed and is down.<br>•**` UP`**—The device is being managed and is up.|
|*** Reachability check**|Determines whether Crosswork Network Controller performs reachability checks on the device. Options<br>are:<br>•**` ENABLE`** (In CSV:**` REACH_CHECK_ENABLE`**)—Checks for reachability and then updates the<br>Reachability State in the user interface automatically.<br>•**` DISABLE`** (In CSV:**` REACH_CHECK_DISABLE`**)—The device reachability check is disabled.<br>Cisco recommends that you always set this to**` ENABLE`**. This field is optional if** Configured State** is<br>marked as**` UNMANAGED`**.|
|**Serial number**|Serial number for the device.|
|**Host name**|The hostname of the device.|



### p285_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**269**|

## Page 286

### p286_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Onboard Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Add devices through the UI**|



### p286_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|**Tags**|The available tags to assign to the device for identification and grouping purposes.<br>Use device tags to group devices for monitoring, and to provide additional information that might be of<br>interest to other users, such as the device’s physical location or its administrator’s email ID.|
|**Software type**|Software type of the device.<br>**Note**<br>Some third-party vendor devices require a specific string to be entered as part of the** Software Type**<br>field. These are the required strings for different vendors:<br>• Juniper devices: JUNOS<br>• Huawei devices: VRP<br>• Nokia devices: TIMOS|
|**Software version**|Software version of the operating system.|
|**UUID**|Universally unique identifier (UUID) for the device.|
|**MAC address**|MAC address of the device.|
|**Inventory ID**|Inventory ID value for the device. The value can contain a maximum of 128 alphanumeric characters,<br>and can include dots (.), underscores ("_"), colons (":"), or hyphens ("-"). No other special characters are<br>allowed.<br>Choose the device host name or an easily identifiable name for Inventory ID as this will be used to sync<br>the device to Crosswork Network Controller with the Inventory ID used as the device name.|
|**Product type**|Product type of the device.|
|**Syslog format**|The format in which syslog events received from the device should be parsed by the syslog collector. The<br>options are:<br>•**` UNKNOWN`** - Choose this option if you are uncertain or if you do not want any parsing to be done by<br>the syslog collector. The Syslog Collection Job output contains syslog events as received from the<br>device.<br>•**` RFC5424`** - Choose this option to parse syslog events received from the device in RFC5424 format.<br>•**` RFC3164`** - Choose this option to parse syslog events received from the device in RFC3164 format.<br>Refer to Section: Syslog Collection Job Output, on page 110 for more details|
|**CLI cache enabled**|Click the checkbox if you wish to enable CLI cache.|
|**Connectivity details**|**Connectivity details**|
|*** Credential Profile**|The name of the credential profile to be used to access the device for data collection and configuration<br>changes. Select the profile for which the device is configured from the dropdown list. For example:**` nso23`**<br>or**` srpce123`**.<br>This field is optional if** Administration State** is marked as**` UNMANAGED`**.|



### p286_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**270**|||

## Page 287

### p287_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Onboard Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Add devices through the UI**||



### p287_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|**Protocol**|The connectivity protocols used by the device. Choices are:**` SNMP`**,**` NETCONF`**,**` TELNET`**,**`HTTP`**,**` HTTPS`**,<br>**`GNMI`**,**` TL1`**, and**` GRPC`**.<br>**Note**<br>Toggle the** Secure Connection** slider to secure the GNMI protocol that you have selected.<br>In this documentation, the secured gNMI protocol is referred to as GNMI_Secure.<br>To add more connectivity protocols for this device, click<br>at the end of the first row in the** Connectivity**<br>**Details** panel. To delete a protocol you have entered, click<br>shown next to that row in the panel.<br>You can enter as many sets of connectivity details as you want, including multiple sets for the same<br>protocol. Enter details for at least**` SSH`** and**` SNMP`**. If you do not configure**` SNMP`**, the device will not be<br>added. If you want to manage the device (or you are managing XR devices), you must enter details for<br>**`NETCONF`**. TELNET connectivity is optional.|
|*** IP Address / Subnet**<br>**Mask**|Enter the device's IP address (IPv4 or IPv6) and subnet mask.<br>**Note**<br>If you have multiple protocols with the same IP address and subnet mask, you can instruct Crosswork<br>Network Controller to autofill the details in the other fields.<br>**Note**<br>Please ensure that the subnets chosen for the IP networks (including devices and destinations) do not<br>have overlapping address space (subnets/supernets) as it may result in unpredictable connectivity issues.|
|*** Port**|The port used for this connectivity protocol.<br>For each protocol enabled on the device, the default port is automatically provided. This default value<br>works correctly in most cases. However, if your network uses non-standard ports, you must update the<br>port settings to match the ones configured in your network.<br>GNMI and GNMI_SECURE: When using gNMI the value is not automatically populated. You must<br>instead enter the value configured on your network devices. The port values range between 57344 to<br>57999. Ensure that the port number you enter here matches with the port number configured on the device.|
|**Timeout**|The elapsed time (in seconds) before communication attempts using this protocol times out. The default<br>value is 30 seconds.<br>While the default value is 30 seconds, a minimum timeout value of 90 seconds is recommended for XE<br>devices using NETCONF. For all other devices and protocols, the recommended minimum timeout value<br>is 60 seconds.|
|**Encoding Type**|This field is only applicable for** GNMI** and** GNMI_SECURE** protocols. The options are**` JSON`**,**` BYTES`**,<br>**`PROTO`**,**` ASCII`**, and**` JSON IETF`**.<br>Based on device capability, only one encoding format is supported at a time in a device.|



### p287_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**271**|

## Page 288

### p288_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Onboard Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Add devices through the UI**|



### p288_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|**Encryption**|This field is applicable only to the SNMP protocol. From the drop-down list, choose the appropriate<br>SNMPv3 protocol supported by the device. The default value is NONE.<br>The drop-down list presents several Advanced Encryption Standard (AES) options, including Counter<br>mode (CTR), Galois/Counter mode (GCM), and Cipher Block Chaining mode (CBC), each supporting<br>various key lengths (128-bit, 192-bit, and 256-bit).<br>The credential profile supports the generic privacy types such as AES-192 and AES-256. For Cisco<br>devices, these are specified as CiscoAES192 and CiscoAES256 protocols.<br>On Cisco devices, the protocols appear as aes256-ctr, aes256-gcm@openssh.com, aes256-cbc, aes192-ctr,<br>and aes192-cbc. To ensure compatibility with Crosswork Network Controller polling, Cisco devices must<br>use these updated protocol variations.<br>On non-Cisco devices, select the encryption that the device supports or use NONE if the device does not<br>use encryption for SNMP.|
|**Trap source IP**|This field is available only when the SNMP protocol is selected.<br>Use this field to specify the source IP address that the device will use to report SNMP traps if it differs<br>from the default management interface IP address.<br>For consistent trap collection, ensure that the IP address entered in the** Trap source IP** field matches the<br>`trap-source` parameter configured on the network device to avoid any issues with SNMP trap handling.<br>**Note**<br>• If the** Trap source IP** field is not specified, Crosswork defaults to using the management interface<br>IP address. For devices added via CSV or API, this field also defaults to the management interface<br>IP address unless explicitly specified.<br>• Ensure that the trap source uses the same IP stack (IPv4 or IPv6) as the device connectivity protocol<br>to maintain consistent communication and avoid mismatches.|
|**SNMP Disable Trap**<br>**Check**|This check box appears when the protocol field is set to**` SNMP`**. Selecting this check box disables the<br>SNMPv2 community string validation between the network device and Data Gateway.<br>Disabling the SNMPv2 community string validation might be a requirement when you want to use a<br>different community string for traps than the one in the credential profile.|
|*** Capability**|The capabilities that allow collection of device data and that are configured on the device. You must select<br>at least**` SNMP`** as this is a required capability. The device will not be onboarded if**` SNMP`** is not configured.<br>Other options are**` YANG_MDT`**,**` YANG_CLI`**,**` TL1`**, and**` GNMI`**. The capabilities that you select will depend<br>on the device software type and version.<br>**Note**<br>• For devices with MDT capability, do not select** YANG_MDT** at this stage.<br>• To enable Crosswork Network Controller to receive the syslog-based data, select** YANG_CLI**.|
|**Providers and access**<br>Provide the provider information.|**Providers and access**<br>Provide the provider information.|
|**Provider family**|Provider type used for topology computation. Choose a provider from the list.|

### p289_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|**Provider name**|Provider name used for topology computation. Choose a provider from the list.<br>**Note**<br>For Cisco NSO LSA deployment, select the resource-facing service (RFS) node to which you want to<br>assign the device.|
|**Credential**|The credential profile used for the provider. This field is read-only and is autopopulated based on the<br>provider you select.|
|**Device key**|The hostname used to link this device record to its corresponding record on the provider. This is typically<br>the device's full hostname, including the domain.|
|**Routing info**|**Routing info**|
|**ISIS system ID**|The device's IS-IS system ID. This ID identifies the router in an IS-IS topology, and is required for SR-PCE<br>integration.<br>This field is a configurable parameter, and cannot be autodiscovered by Crosswork Network Controller.|
|**OSPF router ID**|The device's OSPF router ID. This ID identifies the router in an OSPF topology, and is required for<br>SR-PCE integration.<br>This field is a configurable parameter, and cannot be autodiscovered by Crosswork Network Controller.|
|***TE router ID**|The traffic engineering router ID for the respective IGP.<br>**Note**<br>For visualizing L3 links in topology, devices should be onboarded to Crosswork Network Controller<br>with the** TE Router ID** field populated.|
|**IPv6 router ID**|IPv6 router ID for the device.<br>This field is a configurable parameter, and cannot be autodiscovered by Crosswork Network Controller.|
|**Streaming telemetry config**|**Streaming telemetry config**|
|**VRF**|Name of the VRF within which Model Driven Telemetry (MDT) traffic is routed.|
|**Source interface**|The range of loopback address for the device type. This field is optional. However, we recommend<br>specifying the loopback associated with the VRF by using the selector in the adjacent box.<br>**Note**<br>This field can be edited only when the device is in a DOWN or UNMANAGED state.|
|**Opt out MDT config**|When enabled, Crosswork Network Controller will not push telemetry configuration to the device via<br>NSO. The default setting state is Disabled (which allows Crosswork Network Controller to push telemetry<br>configuration to the device via NSO).<br>The device must be in ADMIN DOWN state to toggle this setting. Any out of band configuration setup<br>must be cleared before moving the setting from Enabled to Disabled.|
|**Location**<br>Provide location information if you want to see your devices on the geographical map.|**Location**<br>Provide location information if you want to see your devices on the geographical map.|

### p295_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Set Up and Use Your Topology Map for Network Visualization|Col2|

|**Overview of the Topology Map**||



### p295_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Callout<br>No.|Description|
|---|---|
|4|**Topology Map**: The topology map can be displayed on a logical map or a geographical map,<br>where the devices and links are shown in their geographic context. From the map, you can drill<br>down to get detailed information about devices and links.<br>**Devices:**<br>• To view basic device information, hover the mouse pointer over the device icon. A pop up<br>window displaying the host name, state, node IP, and device type appears.<br>• To view device details, click on the device icon. For more information see, View Basic<br>Device Details, on page 286<br>If you have installed Element Management Functions:<br>• The following additional information will be displayed in the** Device Details** screen.<br>• Alarm information under Summary in the** Details** tab.<br>•** Interface** tab with name, and operational and admin status for each associated interface.<br>• An** Alarms** tab displaying information such as severity, source, category, and condition<br>of the alarms. The columns can be customized based on your preferences.<br>• An** Inventory** tab displaying the product name, product id, admin status, oper status,<br>and serial number. The columns can be customized based on your preferences.<br>• A** History** tab with detailed information about device performance, including various<br>performance metrics.<br>**Note**<br>Relevant performance policies should be created to see the history for a specific device<br>or link.<br>**Links:**<br>• A solid line represents a_ single link_ between two devices. A dashed line represents an<br>_aggregated_ link, which could indicate multiple links, such as several Layer 2 links (two<br>Ethernet links for example) or several Layer 3 links (2 ISIS links) on the same physical link.<br>To configure the dashed link, refer to Differentiate Aggregated Links from Single Links,<br>on page 301.<br>For easy identification, you can color links on the map based on criteria such as link down<br>and utilization. For more information, refer to Differentiate all Down Links, on page 302<br>and Show Link Health by Color, on page 303.<br>• A and Z indicates connecting interfaces.<br>• To view link information details, click on the link, and the** Links** panel is displayed on the<br>right-hand side with information.|

### p296_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

### p296_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Callout<br>No.|Description|
|---|---|
|5|: The logical map shows devices and their links, positioned according to an automatic layout<br>algorithm, ignoring their geographical location. You can change the layout algorithm.<br>: The geographical map shows single devices, device clusters, and links, superimposed on a<br>map of the world. Each device location on the map reflects the device's GPS coordinates (longitude<br>and latitude) as defined in the device inventory.<br>: The Display Preferences window allows you to change display settings for devices, links.<br>You can also change the display preferences for the alarms by enabling alarm visualization using<br>the** Show Alarms** option in the** Alarms** tab and set a severity filter to show only the alarms of<br>the selected severity or higher. Once enabled, the alarm notification icon will be displayed on<br>the devices in the topology map in case of an alarm.<br>**Note**<br>Settings changes only apply to the current session and will revert to the defaults when you log<br>out and log in again. To retain your changes for future use, save your view before logging out.<br>: The global search allows you to search the topology using device names, location or the<br>device civic location.|
|6|**Expand/Collapse/Hide Side Panel**: Expand or collapse the contents of the side panel. Close the<br>side panel to get a larger view of the topology map.|
|7|The** Mini Dashboard** provides a summary of the IP Domain and device reachability status. If<br>filters are applied, the** Mini Dashboard** is updated to reflect what is displayed in the Devices<br>table.<br>**Note**<br>If you have installed Element Management Functions, the** Alarm Severity** information is<br>displayed in the Mini Dashboard and a** Severity** column is added to the Devices table. You can<br>refine the table based on the severity value.<br>The** Alarm severity** section under the** Details** tab summarizes alarms by category. Click on a<br>category to view the devices associated with those alarms. To see the number of alarms for a<br>specific device, click its host name. The** Summary** will display the total alarms for that device.<br>For a more detailed view, click the** Alarms** tab to access more alarm information.|
|8|The content of this window changes depending on what applications you have installed, what<br>**Show** is set to for the topology map and if you have selected to view more information on the<br>device.|
|9|**Saved Views**: Lets you create a named custom view using the settings and layout for your current<br>map, settings of the tables saved in the saved views, or display a custom view you have created<br>previously.|

### p311_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Link Type|Discovery|Link State|
|---|---|---|
|L2 link (CDP, LLDP,<br>LAG)|via SNMP MIB: CDP, LLDP and<br>LAG|The link state is based on the two link<br>endpoints operational states (via IF MIB).<br>• Link state is UP when initially<br>discovered.<br>• When one of the endpoint interfaces is<br>operationally down, then the link state<br>is set to DOWN.<br>• When both endpoint interfaces are<br>operationally up, then the link state is<br>set to UP.<br>• When one direction of a link is<br>operational while the other direction is<br>down, then the link state is set as<br>degraded.|



### p311_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Protocol/Method|Provides|Use Cases|
|---|---|---|
|IGP/ BGP-LS (via<br>SR-PCE)|Real time topology (nodes, links,<br>link metrics, and so on.)|L3 topology visualization|
|PCEP (via SR-PCE)|Real time LSP status and CRUD<br>of SR-PCE initiated LSPs|• SR/SRv6, RSVP-TE LSP visualization<br>• SR-PCE initiated LSP<br>create/update/delete|
|SNMP (SNMPv2-MIB,<br>IP-MIB, IF-MIB,<br>LLDP-MIB, (CISCO<br>CDP-MIB) (via CDG)|System info, interface table<br>(interface and SR-TE/RSVP-TE<br>traffic Utilization) IP address table,<br>L2 adjacency information|Device management and details and<br>Crosswork Optimization Engine model<br>building:<br>• L2/L3 topology<br>• Interface name, admin/oper status<br>• Interface and SR policy and RSVP-TE<br>tunnel utilization|
|CLI (via CDG) - show<br>mpls|TE router ID and so on.|To match the DLM node with the same TE<br>router ID that is learned from the SR-PCE|

|LAG|cw.topo_svc|`cw.toposvc.lag`|`IF-MIB, LAG-MIB`|`IEEE8023 - LAG -`<br>`MIB : IEEE8023 -`<br>`LAG - MIB /`<br>`dot3adAggTable /`<br>`dot3adAggEntry`<br>`IEEE8023 - LAG -`<br>`MIB : IEEE8023 -`<br>`LAG - MIB /`<br>`dot3adAggPortTable`<br>`/`<br>`dot3adAggPortEntry`|



### p313_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Possible Error Scenario|Cause|Cause Recommended Action|
|---|---|---|
|After disabling, some of the<br>disabled links are displayed in the<br>maps.|A protocol that is disabled soon<br>after being enabled may cause a<br>problem. The system may stop the<br>collection job for the previous<br>enabled job before it finishes<br>processing the SNMP data. This<br>may lead to a mismatch between<br>the actual and the displayed status<br>of the links. The links that are<br>disabled may still appear as<br>enabled.|Enable and disable the protocol<br>again with sufficient wait time in<br>between, or restart robot-topo-svc.<br>To restart the robot-topo-svc, refer<br>to Monitor Platform Infrastructure<br>and Application Health.|



### p313_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**297**|

## Page 314

### p314_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Set Up and Use Your Topology Map for Network Visualization|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Import and Export Geographical Data**|



### p314_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Possible Error Scenario|Cause|Cause Recommended Action|
|---|---|---|
|When you try to enable discovery,<br>the helios job fails and settings are<br>disabled from further editing.|A possible cause of the collection<br>job being stuck in an unsuccessful<br>state is that the helios pod is<br>unhealthy. Crosswork prevents<br>users from modifying the L2<br>discovery settings while the<br>collection job is in progress. This<br>means that the collection job cannot<br>be canceled or restarted until the<br>helios pod is healthy again.|Ensure that the pods are healthy,<br>and then enable and disable the<br>protocol with sufficient wait time<br>in between,or restart<br>robot-topo-svc.<br>To restart the robot-topo-svc, refer<br>to Monitor Platform Infrastructure<br>and Application Health.|
|When you change the discovery<br>settings, the topology UI or<br>topology service crashes resulting<br>in an unpredictable status.|The mechanism to disable users<br>from further editing while the<br>collection job is being created or<br>deleted, relies on pods<br>communicating via Postgres flag.<br>If any pod crashes during this time,<br>the Postgres flag key is not set<br>correctly.|The mechanism to disable users<br>from further editing while the<br>collection job is being created or<br>deleted, relies on pods<br>communicating via Postgres flag.<br>If any pod crashes during this time,<br>the Postgres flag key is not set<br>correctly.|

## Page 342

### p342_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Licenses|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Authorization status responses**|



### p342_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Registration status|License<br>authorization status|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Unregistered|Evaluation mode|A 90-day evaluation period during which the licensed features<br>of Cisco Crosswork Network Controller can be freely used. This<br>state is initiated when you use Cisco Crosswork Network<br>Controller for the first time.|
|Unregistered|Evaluation Expired|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller has not been successfully<br>registered at the end of the evaluation period. During this state,<br>the Cisco Crosswork Network Controller features are disabled,<br>and you must register to continue using the product.|
|Unregistered|Registered Expired|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller is unable to contact the<br>CSSM before the expiration of Identity Certificates and has<br>returned to the unregistered state. Cisco Crosswork Network<br>Controller resumes the remaining evaluation period, if available.<br>At this stage, new registration ID token is required to reregister<br>the product.|
|Registered|Authorized (In<br>Compliance)|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller has been fully authorized<br>to use the reserved licensed features. The authorization is<br>automatically renewed every 30 days.|
|Registered|Out of Compliance|The associated Virtual Account does not have enough licenses<br>to reserve for Cisco Crosswork Network Controller’s current<br>feature use. You must renew the entitlement or usage limit<br>registered with the token to continue using Cisco Crosswork<br>Network Controller.|
|Registered|Authorization<br>Expired|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller is unable to communicate<br>with the CSSM for 90 days or more, and the authorization has<br>expired.|



### p342_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Registration status|License<br>authorization status|Enforced action or message|
|---|---|---|
|Registered|Out of compliance|No action taken. A message is logged with license state indicating<br>that "License usage has exceeded the limit".|



### p342_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**326**|||

### p371_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage System Access and Security|Col2|

|**Global API Permissions**||



### p371_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Category|Global API<br>Permissions|Description|
|---|---|---|
|AAA|Password<br>Change|Provides permission to manage passwords. The READ and WRITE<br>permissions are automatically enabled by default. The DELETE<br>permission is not applicable to the password change operation (You<br>cannot delete a password, you can only change it.)|
|AAA|Remote<br>Authentication<br>Servers<br>Integration|Provides permission to manage remote authentication server<br>configurations in Crosswork. You must have READ permission to<br>view/read configuration, and WRITE permission to add/update the<br>configuration of any external authentication server (e.g. LDAP,<br>TACACS) into Crosswork. The Delete permissions are not applicable<br>for these APIs.|
|AAA|Users and Roles<br>Management|Provides permission to manage users, roles, sessions, and password<br>policies. Supported operations include "Create new user/role", "Update<br>user/role", "Delete a user/role", "Update task details for a user/role",<br>"Session management (Idle-timeout, max session..)", "update password<br>policy”, “get password tooltip help text”, “get active sessions”, etc.<br>The READ permission allows you to view the content.<br>The WRITE permission allows you to create and update.<br>The DELETE permission allows you to delete a user or role.|
|AAA|Know my role -<br>Read only|Enables the logged in users to understand their permissions, or get new<br>permissions.<br>WRITE and DELETE permissions are not applicable for these APIs.|
|AAA|User Preferences|Allows you to manage the dashlets in the homepage.<br>The READ permission allows you to view dashboards, WRITE<br>permission allows your to edit dashboards, DELETE permission allows<br>you to delete dashboards.|
|Administrative<br>Operations|External Kafka|Allows you to subscribe or unsubscribe the external kafka notification<br>streaming.<br>The READ permission allows you to view the list of subscriptions.<br>The WRITE and DELETE permissions allows you to edit and delete<br>the subscriptions respectively.|
|Administrative<br>Operations|RESTCONF<br>Notification<br>Subscription|Allows you to subscribe or unsubscribe the RESTCONF notification<br>streaming (websocket and connectionless).<br>The READ permission allows you to view the list of subscriptions.<br>The WRITE and DELETE permissions allows you to edit and delete<br>the subscriptions respectively.|

||**Global API Permissions**|



### p376_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Category|Global API<br>Permissions|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Collection Infra|Collection APIs|Permissions for APIs to manage collection jobs.<br>Based on the READ/WRITE/DELETE permissions, you can view<br>collection jobs, create/update new collection jobs (external), or delete<br>existing collection jobs. System collection jobs (data collection setup<br>internally for Crosswork consumption) cannot be modified irrespective<br>of these permissions (permitted for Administrators only), but users with<br>the READ permission will be able to view the details of all collection<br>jobs including system collection jobs.<br>For most users, READ-only permissions would be enough as it enables<br>them to view Collection jobs detail (request and status) and actual data<br>collection status/metrics per device/sensor path level.|
|Collection Infra|Data Gateway<br>Manager APIs|Permissions to perform CRUD operations on Destinations, Data<br>Gateways, Custom Packages, etc.<br>The READ permission allows you to view the data, while the WRITE<br>permission allows you to perform these actions:<br>• Add, edit, or delete Data Gateways and Data Gateway instances.<br>• View the vitals<br>• Add, edit, delete, and view the custom packages<br>• View the system packages<br>• Add, edit, or delete data destinations<br>• Update resources<br>• Create, edit, or delete Data Gateway pools<br>• Revoke the provisioning permission from task permissions<br>• Restrict user access by revoking the Inventory API, Data gateway<br>APIs, and Platform APIs permissions.<br>• Troubleshoot data collection issues|
|Collection Infra|Interface Data<br>Collection|Permissions to enable the Crosswork Data Gateway collect the interface<br>state and stats data such as name, type, and traffic counters from the<br>devices through the SNMP or gNMI, or both protocols.<br>The READ permission allows you to view devices configured for SNMP,<br>gNMI, or both protocols. The WRITE permission allows you to<br>configure the data collection by selecting the method or protocol to be<br>used, choosing the relevant device tags, and setting the interval at which<br>data collection requests are sent.|

|Category|Global API<br>Permissions|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Service Health|Archiver APIs|The READ permission allows you to<br>• Check if Historical Data exists for a given service.<br>• Get the Historical Timeline series for a given service.<br>• Get a Service Graph for a selected timestamp of the service.<br>• Retrieve probe and 24 hours metric data for a given service.<br>The WRITE/DELETE permissions are not applicable for these APIs.|
|Service Health|Assurance<br>Graph Manager<br>APIs|The READ permission allows you to:<br>• Fetch details of a service.<br>• Get the impacted list of services.<br>• Retrieve the list of matching sub-services (transport or device only).<br>The WRITE/DELETE permissions are not applicable for these APIs.|
|Service Health|CAT SH UI|The READ permission allows you to:<br>• Retrieve service data, including the total number of monitored<br>services, the count of basic services, and the count of advanced<br>services.<br>• Retrieve the number of services based on health status (for example,<br>Good, Degraded, Down, Error, Initiated, and Paused).<br>• Retrieve the number of provisioned and monitored services<br>categorized by service type (L2 and L3).<br>The WRITE/DELETE permissions are not applicable for these API.|
|Service Health|Config Manager<br>APIs|The READ permission allows you to:<br>• Retrieve advanced and total counts of services with monitoring<br>enabled and published.<br>• Force reconciliation with ISTP.<br>The WRITE permission allows you to update the maximum number of<br>services supported for Total and Advanced monitoring.<br>The DELETE permission is not applicable for these APIs.|
|Service Health|Heuristic<br>Package<br>Manager APIs||



### p383_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

## Page 402

### p402_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage System Access and Security|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Manage TACACS+ Servers**|



### p402_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|Authentication order|Specify a unique priority value to assign precedence in the authentication request. The<br>order can be any number between 10 to 99. Below 10 are system reserved.<br>By default, 10 is selected.|
|IP address|Enter the IP address of the TACACS+ server (if IP address is selected).|
|DNS name|Enter the DNS name (if DNS name is selected). Only IPv4 DNS name is supported.|
|Port|The default TACACS+ port number is 49.|
|Shared secret format|Shared secret for the active TACACS+ server. Select ASCII or Hexadecimal.|
|Shared secret / Confirm<br>shared secret|Plain-text shared secret for the active TACACS+ server. The format of the text entered<br>must match with the format selected (ASCII or Hexadecimal).<br>For Crosswork to communicate with the external authentication server, the** Shared**<br>**Secret** parameter you enter on this screen must match with the shared secret value<br>configured on the TACACS+ server.|



### p402_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**386**|||



---

## Page 403

### p403_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage System Access and Security|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Manage TACACS+ Servers**||



### p403_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Field|Description|
|---|---|
|Service|Enter the value of the service you are attempting to gain access to. This field is verified<br>only for standalone TACACS+. In case of Cisco ISE, you can enter any value; do not<br>leave the field blank.<br>The service field is an attribute that tells the TACACS+ server what type of network<br>service the user is trying to access. It allows the TACACS+ server to distinguish<br>between different types of access, such as:<br>•** Login access** (e.g., device CLI, SSH, console)<br>•** Network access** (e.g., PPP, SLIP)<br>For example, the "`raccess`" value is a service type used in the service field of an<br>authorization request. It stands for** Remote Access** and is typically used when a user<br>is requesting remote administrative access.|
|Policy ID|Enter the user role that you created in the TACACS+ server. The** Policy ID** is a unique<br>key used by the TACACS+ server to identify and retrieve the user role assigned to an<br>authenticated user. This value must exactly match the user role you configured on the<br>TACACS+ server.<br>In Crosswork Network Controller, this field corresponds to the_ policy_id_.<br>**Note**<br>If you try to login to Crosswork Network Controller as a TACACS+ user before<br>creating the required user role, you will get the error message:` "Key not`<br>`authorized: no matching policy"`. If this occurs, close the browser. Login<br>as a local admin user and create the missing user roles in the TACACS+ server, and<br>login back to Crosswork using the TACACS+ user credentials.|
|Device access group<br>attribute|Enter the device access group attribute value based on the key used for the device<br>access group in the (ISE/Standalone) TACACS+ server attributes. These values can<br>be one or more comma-separated entries.<br>In a TACACS+ context, the Device Access Group attribute is typically a custom or<br>authorization attribute that the TACACS+ server sends back to the network device.<br>This attribute specifies which group of network devices or which level of device access<br>policy applies to the authenticated user. The Device Access Group attribute works in<br>sync with the policy id to define user permissions across devices.|
|Retransmit timeout|Enter the timeout value. Maximum timeout is 30 seconds.|
|Retries|Specify the number of authentication retries allowed.|
|Authentication type|Select the authentication type for TACACS+:<br>• PAP: Password-based authentication is the protocol where two entities share a<br>password in advance and use the password as the basis of authentication.<br>• CHAP: Challenge-Handshake Authentication Protocol requires that both the client<br>and server know the plain text of the secret, although it is never sent over the<br>network. CHAP provides greater security than Password Authentication Protocol<br>(PAP).|



### p403_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Crosswork Network Controller 7.1 Administration Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**387**|
